I deliberately chose three hotels not only to experience different styles, but also to have a professional pk to find faults.

      A brief introduction to the preliminary evaluation:
1. Hardware 4 stars:
1) The decoration of guest rooms and public areas uses exquisite materials and fine workmanship. Thumbs up. The layout of the lobby is a bit messy and unsatisfactory.
2) The 24-hour fitness center is good, and the boxing ring is a highlight. Thumbs up. The hotel does not have a swimming pool, unfortunately.
3) The walkway and elevator hall on the second floor are too much space, bad review! Why can't the space be given to the guest room like on the third floor? Is it just to widen the room size difference? Because the room is too large, the actual space inside the Hilton Canopy room is much smaller than that of the Sofitel Legend and W rooms of the same size, and the price/performance ratio is low.
4) The window area of ‚Äã‚Äãthe guest room is not small, but there are opaque vertical *****s on the outer glass, resulting in a poor viewing experience. (If it is to protect the privacy of the guest room, single-sided light-transmitting glass can be used)

Service 4 stars:
1) The front desk mm assisted in meeting the guests' additional requests (upgraded rooms and children's breakfast, and assisted the guests to visit other standard rooms). Thank you to the front desk mm and the manager on duty. Thumbs up. However, when the front desk mm faces these additional demands from guests, she suggests that the hotel can provide more authorization or respond more flexibly and professionally, and the guests may feel better.
2) In the breakfast buffet, can guests take food away? The hotel should have a clear management standard and response measures. I seemed to vaguely hear a supervisor in the breakfast room complaining that takeout service should not be provided.

Location 4 stars:
